</p><p><a href="/wiki/George_Stephenson" title="George Stephenson">George Stephenson</a> (9 June 1781 – 12 August 1848) was an English civil engineer and mechanical engineer who built the first public inter-city railway line in the world to use steam locomotives. Renowned as the father of railways<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> George Stephenson was born in Wylam, Northumberland, 9.3 miles (15.0 km) west of Newcastle upon Tyne.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Swan" title="Joseph Swan">Sir Joseph Wilson Swan</a> (31 October 1828 – 27 May 1914) was a British physicist and chemist from Sunderland, County Durham now the (City of Sunderland). He is most famous for inventing an <a href="/wiki/Incandescent_light_bulb" title="Incandescent light bulb">incandescent light bulb</a> before its invention by the American <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Thomas Edison</a>. Swan first demonstrated the light bulb at a lecture the <a href="/wiki/Literary_and_Philosophical_Society_of_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Literary and Philosophical Society of Newcastle upon Tyne">Literary and Philosophical Society</a> and <a class="external text" href="http://www.mininginstitute.org.uk/aboutus/" rel="nofollow">Miners Institute</a> on <a href="/wiki/History_of_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="History of Newcastle upon Tyne">Mosley Street</a>, Newcastle upon Tyne on 18 December 1878. Mosley Street, Newcastle upon Tyne is reputed to be the first street in the world to be lit by <a href="/wiki/Electric_light" title="Electric light">electric light</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Turbinia_At_Speed.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1408" data-file-width="2000" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Turbinia_At_Speed.jpg/200px-Turbinia_At_Speed.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Turbinia_At_Speed.jpg/300px-Turbinia_At_Speed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Turbinia_At_Speed.jpg/400px-Turbinia_At_Speed.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Turbinia_At_Speed.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Turbinia </i></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charles_Algernon_Parsons" title="Charles Algernon Parsons">Charles Algernon Parsons</a> invented the steam turbine in 1884, and having foreseen its potential to power ships he set up the Parsons Marine Steam Turbine Company with five associates in 1893. To develop this he had the experimental vessel <a href="/wiki/Turbinia" title="Turbinia"><i>Turbinia</i></a> built in a light design of steel by the firm of Brown and Hood, based at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wallsend_on_Tyne" title="Wallsend on Tyne">Wallsend on Tyne</a>. He also pioneered in the field of <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">electricity generation</a>, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_and_District_Electric_Lighting_Company" title="Newcastle and District Electric Lighting Company">Newcastle and District Electric Lighting Company</a> in 1889. The company opened the first power station in the world to generate electricity using <a href="/wiki/Turbo_generator" title="Turbo generator">turbo generators</a> in 1890, at <a href="/wiki/Forth_Banks_Power_Station" title="Forth Banks Power Station">Forth Banks</a> in Newcastle.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_George_Armstrong" title="William George Armstrong">William George Armstrong</a>, 1st Baron Armstrong, CB, FRS (26 November 1810 – 27 December 1900) was an effective Tyneside industrialist who founded the Armstrong Whitworth manufacturing empire. He was responsible for the development of the hydraulic crane and many military armaments. His house at <a href="/wiki/Cragside" title="Cragside">Cragside</a>, Northumberland was the first in the world to be lit by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydro-electricity" title="Hydro-electricity">hydro-electricity</a>, using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incandescent_lamps" title="Incandescent lamps">incandescent lamps</a> provided by the inventor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Swan" title="Joseph Swan">Joseph Swan</a>.
</p><p>In 1936 the first commercially viable production of acrylic safety glass, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perspex" title="Perspex">Perspex</a>, began by ICI Acrylics and the material is still manufactured in the region by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lucite" title="Lucite">Lucite International</a> now part of <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Corporation" title="Mitsubishi Corporation">Mitsubishi Corporation</a>. During the Second World War acrylic glass was used for submarine periscopes, windshields, canopies, and gun turrets for airplanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Shortages in raw materials and price pressures have led to innovation by Lucite who developed their patented Alpha Technology in this region. This technology is now the leading technology used in the manufacture of acrylics around the world. It uses new feedstock's and has a cost advantage of 40% over conventional processing methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a> was the first in the UK and the second in Europe to receive a licence to perform research on stem cells and is a leading centre for such research today. Dr <a href="/wiki/Karim_Nayernia" title="Karim Nayernia">Karim Nayernia</a> was the first to isolate spermatagonial stem cells at this University. Many new healthcare developments have arisen from this stem cell expertise in the region.
</p><p>Today the region has five universities with a number of research departments:
<a href="/wiki/Durham_University" title="Durham University">Durham University</a>, Newcastle University, <a href="/wiki/Northumbria_University" title="Northumbria University">Northumbria University</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sunderland" title="University of Sunderland">University of Sunderland</a> and Teesside University, which have a portfolio of many innovative businesses that have spun out of their research and teaching departments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Businesses">Businesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Businesses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_support_organisations_in_the_region">Business support organisations in the region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Business support organisations in the region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Businesses in Northeast England are supported by a chamber of commerce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The <a class="external text" href="http://www.necc.co.uk/%20North%20East%20Chamber%20of%20Commerce" rel="nofollow">Northeast Chamber of Commerce</a> (NECC)is based in Durham and has active sub committees working in all sub regions.
</p><p>To further encourage <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Small_%26_medium_enterprises" title="Small &amp; medium enterprises">SMEs</a> in the North East of England to Export, the Northeast Process Industry Cluster (NEPIC) has collaborated with the Northeast Chamber of Commerce (NECC) and <a class="external text" href="http://www.rtcnorth.co.uk" rel="nofollow">RTC North Limited</a> to create a jointly owned subsidiary company <a class="external text" href="http://www.nepic.co.uk/media_centre/news/details.asp?ntag=1498" rel="nofollow">Go Global Limited</a> to manage the contract they have to deliver the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UKTI" title="UKTI">United Kingdom Trade &amp; Investment</a> (UKTI), Government funded, support products and programme for all business sectors in their region. The <a class="external text" href="http://www.ukti.gov.uk/export/howwehelp.html" rel="nofollow">UKTI business support products</a>, to help grow international trade, are focused on supporting individual SMEs to grow their exports and they also support Trade Missions to new markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Northern Business Forum is an organisation created in the region to share knowledge and best practice between membership based business support organisations in the Northeast of England. The Forum creates a single voice for business when this is needed. This business led forum also links its member organisations to wider business issues, both locally and nationally, through the local and national business membership organisations that are also represented. Members of the forum include NECC, NEPIC, the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Small_Businesses" title="Federation of Small Businesses">Federation of Small Businesses</a> (FSB), <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_British_Industry" title="Confederation of British Industry">Confederation of British Industry</a> (CBI)North East, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Engineering_Employers_Federation" title="Engineering Employers Federation">Engineering Employers Federation</a> Northern (EEF), The <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Directors" title="Institute of Directors">Institute of Directors</a> (IOD), The <a class="external text" href="http://www.necc.co.uk/" rel="nofollow">North East Chamber of Commerce</a> (NECC),<a class="external text" href="http://www.service-network.co.uk/" rel="nofollow">Service Network</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.rtcnorth.co.uk/ga/" rel="nofollow">RTC North</a> and NEPIC. The <a href="/wiki/Association_of_North_East_Councils" title="Association of North East Councils">Association of North East Councils</a> (ANEC) are amongst the observers of the forum.
</p><p>Businesses investing in the region are supported by the Local Enterprise Partnerships Tees Valley Unlimited (TVU) and the North East Local Enterprise Partnership (NELEP). Both these organisations manage <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enterprise_zone" title="Enterprise zone">enterprise zones</a> to encourage new business investors. There are also several Industry and Business led Cluster bodies in the region to network and engage companies on a sector basis and give local business-to-business advice and supply chain intelligence: the Northeast of England Process Industry Cluster (NEPIC) (chemicals-polymers-pharmaceuticals-biotech), the <a class="external text" href="http://www.nofenergy.co.uk/" rel="nofollow">Northern Offshore Federation</a> (NOF) (energy and offshore engineering), <a class="external text" href="http://www.service-network.co.uk/" rel="nofollow">Service Network</a> (accountants-finance-law firms-HR) and <a class="external text" href="http://www.ndi.org.uk/" rel="nofollow">Northern Defence Industries</a> (NDI) (defence related engineering), <a class="external text" href="http://www.designnetworknorth.org/" rel="nofollow">Design Network North</a> (DNN) (design issues for all sectors.)
</p><p>RTC North provide business expertise in specific growth areas such as product innovation, market research, technology transfer, commercialisation, business growth. North East Access to Finance (NEA2F) operates a business growth fund to help small and medium-sized businesses (SMES).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enterprise_zones">Enterprise zones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Enterprise zones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The North East Enterprise Zone, initiated by the North East Local Enterprise Partnership, was announced by the government in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pearson_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pearson-79">[79]</a></sup> The zone focuses on technology for low carbon vehicle development, marine offshore and subsea engineering, petrochemicals and renewable energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-echo_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-echo-80">[80]</a></sup> At the time of announcement the enterprise zone included two clusters of sites, an Ultra Low Carbon Vehicle zone in Sunderland and a zone on the River Tyne North Bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pearson_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pearson-79">[79]</a></sup> The Sunderland cluster is close to the Nissan plant and includes Turbine Business Park. It hosts <a href="/wiki/Gateshead_College" title="Gateshead College">Gateshead College</a>'s Future Technology Centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-echo_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-echo-80">[80]</a></sup> The cluster on the Tyne includes the Port of Tyne North Estate, Swan Hunter in North Tyneside, and Neptune Yard in Newcastle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pearson_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-Pearson-79">[79]</a></sup> The zone was launched in April 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-echo_80-2"><a href="#cite_note-echo-80">[80]</a></sup> In that year another cluster of sites, comprising the Blyth Estuary Renewable Energy Zone at <a href="/wiki/Blyth,_Northumberland#Port_of_Blyth" title="Blyth, Northumberland">Port of Blyth</a>, was added to the zone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The enterprise zone contains ten sites over the three clusters, covering 115 hectares (280 acres) in total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is also an enterprise zone in Teesside, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tees_Valley_Enterprise_Zone" title="Tees Valley Enterprise Zone">Tees Valley Enterprise Zone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teesside">Teesside</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Teesside">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Industrial_Teesside_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1709361.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="847" data-file-width="1280" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Industrial_Teesside_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1709361.jpg/220px-Industrial_Teesside_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1709361.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Industrial_Teesside_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1709361.jpg/330px-Industrial_Teesside_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1709361.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Industrial_Teesside_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1709361.jpg/440px-Industrial_Teesside_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1709361.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Industrial_Teesside_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1709361.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_BOC_Group" title="The BOC Group">BOC</a> plant on Teesside</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Teesport" title="Teesport">Teesport</a> on the River Tees is the third biggest port in the country in terms of tonnage shipped, largely due to the local steel and chemical industries. <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Chemical_Industries" title="Imperial Chemical Industries">Imperial Chemical Industries</a> (ICI) operated here until the late 1990s on three chemical sites at Wilton, Billingham and Seal Sands. ICI was broken up, and its many chemical manufacturing units are now operated by a large number of companies that have acquired its assets. The Centre for Process Innovation (CPI), a national innovation catapult<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, is based at the Wilton Centre, the former corporate headquarters of ICI, which has become a multi-company research and development centre: along with CPI there are now some 60 other companies, including the cluster body NEPIC, using these R&amp;D and business development facilities. This centre is now one of Europe's largest R&amp;D facilities focusing on developments in the chemistry-based process industries. The area is a chemicals processing area, but recently it has diversified to become the UK's leading site for renewable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biofuel_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Biofuel in the United Kingdom">biofuel</a> research. This industrial activity is taking place in a collaborative environment facilitated by the economic cluster body, the North East of England Process Industry Cluster (NEPIC).
</p><p>Hartlepool has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hartlepool_nuclear_power_station" title="Hartlepool nuclear power station">nuclear power station</a>, and there is a conventional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilton_Power_Station" title="Wilton Power Station">CHP power station</a> and a biomass power station operated by Sembcorp on the Wilton chemical site.<a class="external text" href="http://hfg.heerema.com/content/yards/heerema-hartlepool-uk/" rel="nofollow">Hereema Fabrication Group</a> make North Sea platforms at the A1048/<a href="/wiki/A179_road" title="A179 road">A179</a> roundabout in Hartlepool. <a class="external text" href="http://www.wiltonengineering.co.uk/" rel="nofollow">Wilton Engineering's</a> 50 acre fabrication and maintenance site is in <a href="/wiki/Port_Clarence" title="Port Clarence">Port Clarence</a>. <a href="/wiki/Barker_and_Stonehouse" title="Barker and Stonehouse">Barker and Stonehouse</a> make furniture north of Middlesbrough next to the A66/<a href="/wiki/A178_road" title="A178 road">A178</a> junction, and <a href="/wiki/PD_Ports" title="PD Ports">PD Ports</a>, who own Teesport, the third biggest port in the UK, is headquartered in Middlesbrough adjacent to Middlesbrough railway station. The <a href="/wiki/Teesside_Steelworks" title="Teesside Steelworks">Teesside Steelworks</a> near Redcar has the biggest blast furnace in Europe and is operated by <a class="external text" href="http://www.ssi-steel.co.uk/" rel="nofollow">Sahaviriya Steel Industries</a> (SSI). <a href="/wiki/Tata_Steel_Europe" title="Tata Steel Europe">Tata Steel Europe</a> operate a pipe works at Hartlepool, a heavy beam mill near Middlesbrough and a special sections mill at <a href="/wiki/Skinningrove_Steelworks" title="Skinningrove Steelworks">Skinningrove Steelworks</a>. <a href="/wiki/Able_UK" title="Able UK">Able UK</a> operate the biggest <a href="/wiki/Dry_dock" title="Dry dock">dry dock</a> in the UK near Seaton Carew, Hartlepool where ships can be dismantled and oil rigs can be dismantled or refurbished.
</p><p>The many chemistry-based businesses on Teesside<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> include <a href="/wiki/Huntsman_Corporation" title="Huntsman Corporation">Huntsman Tioxide</a> plant at <a href="/wiki/Greatham,_County_Durham" title="Greatham, County Durham">Greatham</a> makes <a href="/wiki/Titanium_dioxide" title="Titanium dioxide">titanium dioxide</a>. Huntsman's European headquarters are in Wynyard. Johnson Matthey Catalysts and Fujifilm Dyosynth Biologics have manufacturing units in Billingham while the Lucite International Acrylics factory and the Mitsubishi battery chemical plant are on the other side of the town. Exwold Technology operate their two extrusion and packaging facilities in Hartlepool. Banner Chemicals are adjacent to the A66 in Middlesbrough. <a href="/wiki/Aldous_Huxley" title="Aldous Huxley">Aldous Huxley</a>'s visit to the former ICI plant in Billingham inspired <i><a href="/wiki/Brave_New_World" title="Brave New World">Brave New World</a></i> and this unit now makes fertiliser for Growhow, using 1% of the UK's natural gas. SABIC perochemicals and polymers, Lotte Chemicals PET and PTA plants, Biffa recycled polymers, Huntsman polyurathanes and the Ensus Biofuels all operate at Wilton. ConocoPhillips refinery, BP Cats, Harvest Energy Biodiesel unit, Greenery Fuels, Fine Organics, Vertelus speciality chemicals and Ineos Nitriles are all based at Seal Sands, with Vopak and Simon Storage tank storage businesses nearby. Air Products are building<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> two waste to energy units at Seal Sands, and Sita are upgrading<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> their unit at Haverton Hill. <a href="/wiki/Premier_Foods" title="Premier Foods">Marlow Foods</a> produce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quorn_(food_product)" title="Quorn (food product)">Quorn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/KP_Snacks" title="KP Snacks">KP Snacks</a> make <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McCoy%27s_Crisps" title="McCoy's Crisps">McCoy's Crisps</a> in Billingham. <a href="/wiki/Santander_UK" title="Santander UK">Santander UK</a>'s mortgages division is located in <a href="/wiki/Thornaby-on-Tees" title="Thornaby-on-Tees">Thornaby-on-Tees</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tetley" title="Tetley">Tetley Tea</a> have had their only <a href="/wiki/Tea_bag" title="Tea bag">tea bag</a> factory in the UK at <a href="/wiki/Eaglescliffe" title="Eaglescliffe">Eaglescliffe</a>, in the borough of Stockton-on-Tees, since 1969. It is the largest tea bag factory in the world and makes 18 billion tea bags a year. Its distribution centre is at nearby <a href="/wiki/Newton_Aycliffe" title="Newton Aycliffe">Newton Aycliffe</a> in County Durham.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tyne_and_Wear">Tyne and Wear</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tyne and Wear">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="List of companies based in Newcastle upon Tyne">List of companies based in Newcastle upon Tyne</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1467801861_ae07518ec0.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="375" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/1467801861_ae07518ec0.jpg/220px-1467801861_ae07518ec0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/1467801861_ae07518ec0.jpg/330px-1467801861_ae07518ec0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e0/1467801861_ae07518ec0.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1467801861_ae07518ec0.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Newcastle Brown Ale – the <i>yen an anny</i> (which means "the one and only" in Tyneside dialect.)</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Offshore_Group_Newcastle" title="Offshore Group Newcastle">Offshore Group Newcastle</a> make <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">oil platforms</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sage_Group" title="Sage Group">Sage Group</a>, who produce <a href="/wiki/Accounting_software" title="Accounting software">accounting software</a>, are based at <a href="/wiki/Hazlerigg" title="Hazlerigg">Hazlerigg</a> at the northern end of the Newcastle bypass. <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rock" title="Northern Rock">Northern Rock</a>, which became a bank in 1997 and was taken over by <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Money_UK" title="Virgin Money UK">Virgin Money</a> in November 2011, and the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Building_Society" title="Newcastle Building Society">Newcastle Building Society</a> are based in <a href="/wiki/Gosforth" title="Gosforth">Gosforth</a>. The Gosforth-based bakery <a href="/wiki/Greggs" title="Greggs">Greggs</a> now has over 1,500 shops. The Balliol Business Park in <a href="/wiki/Longbenton" title="Longbenton">Longbenton</a> contains <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a> research and global business centres and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Working_tax_credit" title="Working tax credit">tax credits</a> call centre for <a href="/wiki/HM_Revenue_and_Customs" title="HM Revenue and Customs">HMRC</a>, and is the former home of <a href="/wiki/Findus" title="Findus">Findus</a> UK. The Government <a href="/wiki/National_Insurance" title="National Insurance">National Insurance</a> Contributions Office in Longbenton, demolished and replaced in 2000, had a 1 mile (1.6 km) long corridor.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Be-Ro" title="Be-Ro">Be-Ro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Go-Ahead_Group" title="Go-Ahead Group">Go-Ahead Group</a> bus company are in central Newcastle. <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a> use the former Rowntrees chocolate factory on the east of the A1. <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Land_%26_Armaments" title="BAE Systems Land &amp; Armaments">BAE Systems Land &amp; Armaments</a> in <a href="/wiki/Benwell_and_Scotswood" title="Benwell and Scotswood">Scotswood</a>, formerly <a href="/wiki/Vickers-Armstrongs" title="Vickers-Armstrongs">Vickers-Armstrongs</a>, is the main producer of <a href="/wiki/Tanks_in_the_British_Army" title="Tanks in the British Army">British Army tanks</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Challenger_2" title="Challenger 2">Challenger 2</a>. A Rolls Royce apprentice training site is next door.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siemens_Power_Generation" title="Siemens Power Generation">Siemens Energy Service Fossil</a> make <a href="/wiki/Steam_turbine" title="Steam turbine">steam turbines</a> at the <a href="/wiki/C._A._Parsons_and_Company" title="C. A. Parsons and Company">CA Parsons Works</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Heaton" title="South Heaton">South Heaton</a>. Sir <a href="/wiki/Charles_Algernon_Parsons" title="Charles Algernon Parsons">Charles Parsons</a> invented the steam turbine in 1884, and developed an important local company. <a href="/wiki/Domestos" title="Domestos">Domestos</a>, a product whose main ingredient is <a href="/wiki/Sodium_hypochlorite" title="Sodium hypochlorite">sodium hypochlorite</a>, was originated in Newcastle in 1929 by William Handley, and was distributed from the area for many years. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rotary_Power&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rotary Power (page does not exist)">Rotary Power</a> make pumps at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=St_Peter%27s,_Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="St Peter's, Newcastle upon Tyne (page does not exist)">St Peter's</a> on the Tyne. 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Clarke_Chapman" title="Clarke Chapman">Clarke Chapman</a> is next to the <a href="/wiki/A167_road" title="A167 road">A167</a> in Gateshead. The <a href="/wiki/MetroCentre_(shopping_centre)" title="MetroCentre (shopping centre)">MetroCentre</a>, the largest shopping centre in Europe, is in <a href="/wiki/Dunston,_Tyne_and_Wear" title="Dunston, Tyne and Wear">Dunston</a>. <a href="/wiki/Scottish_%26_Newcastle" title="Scottish &amp; Newcastle">Scottish &amp; Newcastle</a> was the largest UK-owned brewery until it was bought by Heineken and Carlsberg in April 2008, and produced <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Brown_Ale" title="Newcastle Brown Ale">Newcastle Brown Ale</a> at the Newcastle Federation Brewery in Dunston until production moved to <a href="/wiki/Tadcaster" title="Tadcaster">Tadcaster</a> in September 2010. At <a href="/wiki/Team_Valley" title="Team Valley">Team Valley</a> are <a href="/wiki/De_La_Rue" title="De La Rue">De La Rue</a>, with their largest banknote printing facility, and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Myson_Radiators&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Myson Radiators (page does not exist)">Myson Radiators</a>, the second largest in the UK market. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Petards_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Petards (company) (page does not exist)">Petards</a> make surveillance equipment including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automatic_number_plate_recognition" title="Automatic number plate recognition">ANPR</a> cameras, and its <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Loebl#Joyce,_Loebl_&amp;_Company_Ltd" title="Herbert Loebl">Joyce-Loebl</a> division makes <a href="/wiki/Electronic_warfare" title="Electronic warfare">electronic warfare</a> systems and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Countermeasure_dispensing_system&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Countermeasure dispensing system (page does not exist)">countermeasure dispensing systems</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/AN/ALE-47" title="AN/ALE-47">AN/ALE-47</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sevcon" title="Sevcon">Sevcon</a>, an international company formed from a part of Smith Electric, is a world leader in electric vehicle controls. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=AEI_Cables&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="AEI Cables (page does not exist)">AEI Cables</a> and <a href="/wiki/Komatsu_Limited" title="Komatsu Limited">Komatsu UK</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heavy_equipment_(construction)" title="Heavy equipment (construction)">construction equipment</a> at Birtley.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J._Barbour_%26_Sons" title="J. Barbour &amp; Sons">J. Barbour &amp; Sons</a> make outdoor clothing in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Simonside&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Simonside (page does not exist)">Simonside</a>, Jarrow. <a href="/wiki/Saft_Groupe_S.A." title="Saft Groupe S.A.">SAFT Batteries</a> make primary <a href="/wiki/Lithium_battery" title="Lithium battery">lithium batteries</a> on the B1344 on the Tyne. <a href="/wiki/Bellway" title="Bellway">Bellway plc</a> houses is in <a href="/wiki/Seaton_Burn" title="Seaton Burn">Seaton Burn</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Tyneside" title="North Tyneside">North Tyneside</a>. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cobalt_Business_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cobalt Business Park (page does not exist)">Cobalt Business Park</a>, the largest office park in the UK, is at <a href="/wiki/Wallsend" title="Wallsend">Wallsend</a>, on the former site of <a href="/wiki/Atmel" title="Atmel">Atmel</a>, and is the home of North Tyneside Council. <a href="/wiki/Swan_Hunter" title="Swan Hunter">Swan Hunter</a> until 2006 made ships in Wallsend, and still designs ships. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Soil_Machine_Dynamics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Soil Machine Dynamics (page does not exist)">Soil Machine Dynamics</a> in Wallsend on the Tyne makes <a href="/wiki/Remotely_operated_underwater_vehicle" title="Remotely operated underwater vehicle">Remotely operated underwater vehicles</a>, and its <a href="/wiki/Ultra_Trencher_1" title="Ultra Trencher 1">Ultra Trencher 1</a> is the world's largest submersible robot.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nissan_Motor_Works_from_the_Air_-_geograph.org.uk_-_486110.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Nissan_Motor_Works_from_the_Air_-_geograph.org.uk_-_486110.jpg/220px-Nissan_Motor_Works_from_the_Air_-_geograph.org.uk_-_486110.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Nissan_Motor_Works_from_the_Air_-_geograph.org.uk_-_486110.jpg/330px-Nissan_Motor_Works_from_the_Air_-_geograph.org.uk_-_486110.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Nissan_Motor_Works_from_the_Air_-_geograph.org.uk_-_486110.jpg/440px-Nissan_Motor_Works_from_the_Air_-_geograph.org.uk_-_486110.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nissan_Motor_Works_from_the_Air_-_geograph.org.uk_-_486110.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nissan_Motor_Manufacturing_UK" title="Nissan Motor Manufacturing UK">Nissan UK</a> off the <a href="/wiki/A19_road" title="A19 road">A19</a> near <a href="/wiki/City_of_Sunderland" title="City of Sunderland">Sunderland</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Car_dealership" title="Car dealership">car dealership</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Evans_Halshaw&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Evans Halshaw (page does not exist)">Evans Halshaw</a> is in Sunderland. The car factory owned by <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Motor_Manufacturing_UK" title="Nissan Motor Manufacturing UK">Nissan Motor Manufacturing UK</a> between <a href="/wiki/North_Hylton" title="North Hylton">North Hylton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_Tyne_and_Wear" title="Washington, Tyne and Wear">Washington</a> is the largest in the UK. <a href="/wiki/Grundfos" title="Grundfos">Grundfos</a>, the world's leading pump manufacturer, builds pumps in Sunderland. <a href="/wiki/Calsonic_Kansei" title="Calsonic Kansei">Calsonic Kansei</a> UK, formerly <a href="/wiki/Magna_International" title="Magna International">Magna</a>, make automotive <a href="/wiki/Dashboard" title="Dashboard">instrument panels</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trim_package" title="Trim package">car trim</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Pennywell" title="Pennywell">Pennywell</a> Industrial Estate. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gestamp" title="Gestamp">Gestamp</a> UK make automotive components. <a href="/wiki/Smith_Electric_Vehicles" title="Smith Electric Vehicles">Smith Electric Vehicles</a> originated in Washington. The <a href="/wiki/LG_Electronics" title="LG Electronics">LG Electronics</a> microwave oven factory opened in 1989, closed in May 2004, and later became the site of the <a href="/wiki/Tanfield_Group" title="Tanfield Group">Tanfield Group</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dunlop_Tyres" title="Dunlop Tyres">Goodyear Dunlop</a> had their only UK car tyre factory next to the Tanfield site until its 2006 closure. BAE Systems <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Land_%26_Armaments" title="BAE Systems Land &amp; Armaments">Global Combat Systems</a> moved to a new £75 million factory at the former Goodyear site in 2011, where they make large calibre ammunition for tanks and artillery. The government's <a href="/wiki/Child_benefit" title="Child benefit">child benefit</a> office is in Washington. <a href="/wiki/Liebherr_Group" title="Liebherr Group">Liebherr</a> build cranes next to the Wear at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Deptford,_Sunderland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Deptford, Sunderland (page does not exist)">Deptford</a>. The outdoor clothing company <a href="/wiki/Berghaus" title="Berghaus">Berghaus</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Castletown,_Sunderland" title="Castletown, Sunderland">Castletown</a>. <a href="/wiki/Vaux_Breweries" title="Vaux Breweries">Vaux Breweries</a>, who owned <a href="/wiki/Swallow_Hotels" title="Swallow Hotels">Swallow Hotels</a>, closed in 1999. <a href="/wiki/ScS" title="ScS">ScS</a> Sofas are on Borough Road. There are many call centres in Sunderland, notably <a href="/wiki/EDF_Energy" title="EDF Energy">EDF Energy</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Doxford_International_Business_Park" title="Doxford International Business Park">Doxford International Business Park</a>, which is also the home of the headquarters of the large international transport company <a href="/wiki/Arriva" title="Arriva">Arriva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike UK</a>. Rolls Royce plan to move their production of <a href="/wiki/Components_of_jet_engines" title="Components of jet engines">fan and turbine discs</a> to BAE Systems' new site in 2016.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northumberland">Northumberland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Northumberland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ashington has the <a href="/wiki/Alcan_Lynemouth_Aluminium_Smelter" title="Alcan Lynemouth Aluminium Smelter">Alcan Lynemouth Aluminium Smelter</a>, next to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lynemouth_Power_Station" title="Lynemouth Power Station">Lynemouth Power Station</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hammerite" title="Hammerite">Hammerite</a> and Cuprinol are made in <a href="/wiki/Prudhoe" title="Prudhoe">Prudhoe</a> by <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Chemical_Industries" title="Imperial Chemical Industries">ICI Paints</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a> factory in <a href="/wiki/Seaton_Delaval" title="Seaton Delaval">Seaton Delaval</a> makes <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Boss" title="Hugo Boss">Hugo Boss</a> aftershave and <a href="/wiki/Clairol" title="Clairol">Clairol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nice_%27n_Easy_(hair_coloring)" title="Nice 'n Easy (hair coloring)">Nice 'n Easy</a> hair dye at a site formerly owned by Shultons, who originated <a href="/wiki/Old_Spice" title="Old Spice">Old Spice</a> and were bought by P&amp;G in 1990. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McQuay_International" title="McQuay International">McQuay</a> UK makes air conditioning systems on the Bassington Industrial Estate at the A1068/A1172 junction in <a href="/wiki/Cramlington" title="Cramlington">Cramlington</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Avery_Dennison" title="Avery Dennison">Avery Dennison</a> UK make labels on the Nelson Industrial Estate off of the A192. Schweppes' <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Abbey_Well&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Abbey Well (page does not exist)">Abbey Well</a> mineral water, the official water of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">London 2012 Olympic Games</a>, is made by <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Enterprises" title="Coca-Cola Enterprises">Coca-Cola</a> in the east of <a href="/wiki/Morpeth,_Northumberland" title="Morpeth, Northumberland">Morpeth</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Renewable_Energy_Centre_(Narec)" title="National Renewable Energy Centre (Narec)">National Renewable Energy Centre</a> (Narec) is at Blyth.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="County_Durham_businesses">County Durham businesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: County Durham businesses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Phileas_Fogg_snacks" title="Phileas Fogg snacks">Phileas Fogg snacks</a> are made by the <a href="/wiki/United_Biscuits" title="United Biscuits">United Biscuits</a> subsidiary <a href="/wiki/KP_Snacks" title="KP Snacks">KP Snacks</a> in <a href="/wiki/Consett" title="Consett">Consett</a> on the Number One Industrial Estate. Nearby <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=CAV_Aerospace&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="CAV Aerospace (page does not exist)">CAV Aerospace</a> make <a href="/wiki/Ice_protection_system" title="Ice protection system">ice protection systems</a> for aircraft.  <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Swan" title="Thomas Swan">Thomas Swan</a>, an international chemicals company, is in <a href="/wiki/Crookhall" title="Crookhall">Crookhall</a>. The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Explorer_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Explorer Group (page does not exist)">Explorer Group</a>, who own <a href="/wiki/Elddis" title="Elddis">Elddis</a>, make caravans at <a href="/wiki/Delves_Lane" title="Delves Lane">Delves</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LG_Philips_Display" title="LG Philips Display">LG Philips Displays</a> <a href="/wiki/Cathode_ray_tube" title="Cathode ray tube">cathode ray tube</a> factory at <a href="/wiki/Carrville" title="Carrville">Carrville</a>, Durham was the second largest employer in the north east after Nissan, before the company went bankrupt in 2006. <a href="/wiki/Northumbrian_Water" title="Northumbrian Water">Northumbrian Water</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Pity_Me" title="Pity Me">Pity Me</a>, <a href="/wiki/Framwellgate_Moor" title="Framwellgate Moor">Framwellgate Moor</a>. Esh Group is a large construction company based south of Durham in <a href="/wiki/Bowburn" title="Bowburn">Bowburn</a>. <a href="/wiki/Schmitz_Cargobull" title="Schmitz Cargobull">Schmitz Cargobull</a> UK is the UK's biggest <a href="/wiki/Semi-trailer" title="Semi-trailer">trailer</a> manufacturer, notably for <a href="/wiki/Refrigerator_truck" title="Refrigerator truck">refrigerated trailers</a>, and is based at <a href="/wiki/Harelaw" title="Harelaw">Harelaw</a> near the <a href="/wiki/Pontop_Pike_transmitting_station" title="Pontop Pike transmitting station">Pontop Pike mast</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flymo-e25.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="864" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Flymo-e25.jpg/220px-Flymo-e25.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Flymo-e25.jpg/330px-Flymo-e25.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Flymo-e25.jpg/440px-Flymo-e25.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flymo-e25.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flymos are made in <a href="/wiki/Newton_Aycliffe" title="Newton Aycliffe">Newton Aycliffe</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Black_%26_Decker" title="Black &amp; Decker">Black &amp; Decker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electrolux" title="Electrolux">Electrolux</a> had large factories at <a href="/wiki/Spennymoor" title="Spennymoor">Spennymoor</a>, but moved production overseas. Thorn Lighting of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zumtobel_Lighting_Group" title="Zumtobel Lighting Group">Zumtobel Lighting Group</a> are on the Green Lane Industrial Estate at Spennymoor. Since 2007 <a href="/wiki/RF_Micro_Devices" title="RF Micro Devices">RF Micro Devices</a> (RFMD) have made electronic <a href="/wiki/Wafer_(electronics)" title="Wafer (electronics)">wafers</a> on the Heighington Lane Business Park at <a href="/wiki/Newton_Aycliffe" title="Newton Aycliffe">Newton Aycliffe</a>, on the site formerly owned by <a href="/wiki/Fujitsu" title="Fujitsu">Fujitsu</a>. Slightly to the north, <a href="/wiki/ThyssenKrupp" title="ThyssenKrupp">TKA Tallent</a> make automotive axles and chassis components. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Husqvarna_AB" title="Husqvarna AB">Husqvarna</a>-<a href="/wiki/Flymo" title="Flymo">Flymo</a>, formerly owned by Electrolux, are on the Aycliffe Industrial Estate, where the world's first hover <a href="/wiki/Lawn_mower" title="Lawn mower">mower</a> was built in 1965. In <a href="/wiki/West_Auckland" title="West Auckland">West Auckland</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Potters_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Potters (company) (page does not exist)">Potters Europe</a> make <a href="/wiki/Raised_pavement_marker" title="Raised pavement marker">road reflectors</a>. <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a> has a site at <a href="/wiki/Barnard_Castle" title="Barnard Castle">Barnard Castle</a> that makes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_company" title="Pharmaceutical company">pharmaceuticals</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/NSK_Ltd." title="NSK Ltd.">NSK</a> make ball bearings on the North West Industrial Estate at Peterlee, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GWA_International" title="GWA International">GWA International</a> subsidiary <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gliderol&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gliderol (page does not exist)">Gliderol</a> UK build <a href="/wiki/Garage_door" title="Garage door">garage doors</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mecaplast_Group" title="Mecaplast Group">Mecaplast Group</a> UK produce automotive components on the Low Hills Industrial Estate in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Easington_Village" title="Easington Village">Easington Village</a> near Peterlee. <a href="/wiki/Reckitt_Benckiser" title="Reckitt Benckiser">Reckitt Benckiser</a> make <a href="/wiki/Cough_medicine" title="Cough medicine">cough syrup</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antacid" title="Antacid">indigestion remedies</a> at <a href="/wiki/Old_Shotton" title="Old Shotton">Shotton</a>, near Peterlee until 2014. <a href="/wiki/Walkers_(snack_foods)" title="Walkers (snack foods)">Walkers Crisps</a> have a site north of Peterlee.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tyne_Bridge_and_the_Sage_Gateshead.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1765" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Tyne_Bridge_and_the_Sage_Gateshead.jpg/220px-Tyne_Bridge_and_the_Sage_Gateshead.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Tyne_Bridge_and_the_Sage_Gateshead.jpg/330px-Tyne_Bridge_and_the_Sage_Gateshead.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Tyne_Bridge_and_the_Sage_Gateshead.jpg/440px-Tyne_Bridge_and_the_Sage_Gateshead.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tyne_Bridge_and_the_Sage_Gateshead.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tyne_Bridge" title="Tyne Bridge">Tyne Bridge</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sage_Gateshead" title="The Sage Gateshead">the Sage Gateshead</a></div></div></div>
<p>Darlington stayed relatively un-industrialised throughout the 20th century, with finance and manufacturing as the main elements of its economy. Darlington today is recognised primarily for its railways, as the first steam-hauled public passenger railway in the world was constructed through the town. <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Bridge_%26_Engineering_Company" title="Cleveland Bridge &amp; Engineering Company">Cleveland Bridge &amp; Engineering Company</a>, which is responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Harbour_Bridge" title="Sydney Harbour Bridge">Sydney Harbour Bridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tyne_Bridge" title="Tyne Bridge">Tyne Bridge</a>, is still based in Darlington. The Orange mobile network provider, Argos and Aldi, and the American engineering company <a href="/wiki/Cummins" title="Cummins">Cummins</a> all have sites in Darlington. The town centre continues to develop into a successful retail hub for the region, and a large new £110m shopping centre, 'The Oval', is under construction. The national safeguarding authority has set up its national office here. The <a href="/wiki/Student_Loans_Company" title="Student Loans Company">Student Loans Company</a> has begun operations in <a href="/wiki/Lingfield_Point" title="Lingfield Point">Lingfield Point</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Magnet_Kitchens" title="Magnet Kitchens">Magnet Kitchens</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Lingfield,_County_Durham" title="Lingfield, County Durham">Lingfield</a> east of town.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alf_Common_the_World%27s_first_%C2%A31000_footballer.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="786" data-file-width="400" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Alf_Common_the_World%27s_first_%C2%A31000_footballer.jpg/150px-Alf_Common_the_World%27s_first_%C2%A31000_footballer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Alf_Common_the_World%27s_first_%C2%A31000_footballer.jpg/225px-Alf_Common_the_World%27s_first_%C2%A31000_footballer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Alf_Common_the_World%27s_first_%C2%A31000_footballer.jpg/300px-Alf_Common_the_World%27s_first_%C2%A31000_footballer.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alf_Common_the_World%27s_first_%C2%A31000_footballer.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alf Common of England, the world's first £1000 footballer</div></div></div>
<p>A precursor of modern football is still seen in the region at some annual <a href="/wiki/Shrove_Tuesday" title="Shrove Tuesday">Shrove Tuesday</a> games at <a href="/wiki/Alnwick" title="Alnwick">Alnwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chester-le-Street" title="Chester-le-Street">Chester-le-Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sedgefield" title="Sedgefield">Sedgefield</a> and many of such games have pre-Norman origins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In 1280 at <a href="/wiki/Ulgham" title="Ulgham">Ulgham</a> near <a href="/wiki/Morpeth,_Northumberland" title="Morpeth, Northumberland">Morpeth</a> Northumberland, records show that Henry of Ellington was killed playing football when David Le Keu's knife went into Henry's belly and killed him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Magoun_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Magoun-88">[88]</a></sup> Organised football teams as we know today did not appear until the 1870s. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_Football_Club" title="Middlesbrough Football Club">Middlesbrough Football Club</a> was formed by local cricket players in 1876 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunderland_Association_Football_Club" title="Sunderland Association Football Club">Sunderland Association Football Club</a> in 1879 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_Football_Club" title="Newcastle United Football Club">Newcastle United Football Club</a> was formed in 1892 by uniting Newcastle West End FC with Newcastle East End.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hutchinson_1997_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hutchinson_1997-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>Darlington formed in 1861 (re-formed 1883 and in 2012) and West Hartlepool of 1881 became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hartlepool_United" title="Hartlepool United">Hartlepool United</a> in 1908. In 1888 Sunderland and Middlesbrough were troubled by rival break-away teams called Sunderland Albion and Middlesbrough Ironopolis, both of which were lost before the 20th century began. Sunderland won the league championship three times in the 1890s and Newcastle United were first division champions three times in the early 1900s, reaching the FA Cup Final three times before winning it at the fourth attempt in 1910.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>
Today top quality professional football remains in the northeast of England. In 2017 - 18 season Newcastle United is a <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> team, whilst Middlesbrough and Sunderland are in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" title="Football League Championship">Football League Championship</a>, Hartlepool and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gateshead_FC" title="Gateshead FC">Gateshead FC</a> compete in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_(division)" title="National League (division)">National League</a>.  <a href="/wiki/St_James%27_Park" title="St James' Park">St James' Park</a> in Newcastle, the <a href="/wiki/Stadium_of_Light" title="Stadium of Light">Stadium of Light</a> in Sunderland and <a href="/wiki/Riverside_Stadium" title="Riverside Stadium">The Riverside Stadium</a> in Middlesbrough are all first class football venues often used for international games at all levels.
</p>
<h4><span id="First_.22world_cup.22_winners_and_influential_amateurs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id='First_"world_cup"_winners_and_influential_amateurs'>First "world cup" winners and influential amateurs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title='Edit section: First "world cup" winners and influential amateurs'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Amateur and semi-professional football clubs like <a href="/wiki/Bishop_Auckland_F.C." title="Bishop Auckland F.C.">Bishop Auckland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blyth_Spartans_A.F.C." title="Blyth Spartans A.F.C.">Blyth Spartans A.F.C.</a> have had success and public attention through <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">Football Association Cup</a> runs, but the most famous achievement was by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Auckland_Town_FC" title="West Auckland Town FC">West Auckland Town FC</a> in 1910: they were invited to take part in a competition in Italy to compete for what was then labelled the soccer World Cup. West Auckland won the competition against some of Europe's biggest sides; they defeated the mighty <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juventus" title="Juventus">Juventus</a> 2-0 in the final. They even successfully defended the title the following year. The first world cup trophy played for in these tournaments, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Thomas_Lipton_Trophy" title="Sir Thomas Lipton Trophy">Sir Thomas Lipton Trophy</a>, has an interesting history of its own. In January 1994 the trophy, which was being held in West Auckland Working Men's Club, was stolen and never recovered. An exact replica of the original trophy was commissioned and is now held by West Auckland FC. The story of West Auckland's success was made into a film called "A Captain's Tale", starring actor <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Waterman" title="Dennis Waterman">Dennis Waterman</a> as club captain Jones.
</p><p>Players from some of the region's minor league teams have gone on to influence football on the world stage. <a href="/wiki/Jack_Greenwell" title="Jack Greenwell">Jack Greenwell</a> (John Richard Greenwell), an ex-coal miner who played non-league football for <a href="/wiki/Crook_Town_A.F.C." title="Crook Town A.F.C.">Crook Town A.F.C.</a> from 1901 to 1912, went to Spain and played 88 games for Barcelona before becoming their manager in 1917. Mr Greenwell's achievements at Barcelona include winning five Catalan championships and two <a href="/wiki/Copa_del_Rey" title="Copa del Rey">Copas del Rey</a>. He also managed Espanyol, Mallorca and Valencia. On the outbreak of the Spanish Civil War, he moved to South America to manage the Peruvian and Colombian national teams; he died in 1942 in <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Bogotá</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_footballers_associated_with_the_region">Notable footballers associated with the region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Notable footballers associated with the region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are many notable footballers from the Northeast of England. Sunderland's <a href="/wiki/Alf_Common" title="Alf Common">Alf Common</a> became the world's first £1,000 player when he was signed by Middlesbrough in 1905.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Other pre Second World War and immediate post war greats were <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Buchan" title="Charlie Buchan">Charles Buchan</a>, who created and edited the iconic magazine "Football Monthly",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_Camsell" title="George Camsell">George Camsell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hughie_Gallacher" title="Hughie Gallacher">Hughie Gallacher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilf_Mannion" title="Wilf Mannion">Wilf Mannion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raich_Carter" title="Raich Carter">Raich Carter</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bob_Gurney" title="Bob Gurney">Bob Gurney</a> all of whom are described in a famous book by the "Clown Prince of Football" <a href="/wiki/Len_Shackleton" title="Len Shackleton">Len Shackleton</a>. Mr Shackleton's book shot to immediate fame and caused a storm when first published because chapter 9, named "The Average Director's Knowledge of Football", was produced as a blank page.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Local Heroes after the Second World War included <a href="/wiki/Joe_Harvey" title="Joe Harvey">Joe Harvey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Milburn" title="Jackie Milburn">Jackie Milburn</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brian_Clough" title="Brian Clough">Brian Clough</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> and Newcastle's <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Moncur" title="Bobby Moncur">Bobby Moncur</a> who led his team to win the Inter City Fairs Cup in 1969.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wilf_Mannion_Statue_MFC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1911" data-file-width="1393" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Wilf_Mannion_Statue_MFC.jpg/150px-Wilf_Mannion_Statue_MFC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Wilf_Mannion_Statue_MFC.jpg/225px-Wilf_Mannion_Statue_MFC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Wilf_Mannion_Statue_MFC.jpg/300px-Wilf_Mannion_Statue_MFC.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wilf_Mannion_Statue_MFC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wilf Mannion's Statue at Middlesbrough's Riverside Stadium</div></div></div>
<p>Perhaps the two most significant English players to come from this region are <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Charlton" title="Bobby Charlton">Bobby Charlton</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jackie_Charlton" title="Jackie Charlton">Jackie Charlton</a> who learnt their early football after being born and raised in the coal mining town of <a href="/wiki/Ashington" title="Ashington">Ashington</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> They were incidentally related to Jackie Milburn who was their uncle. Bobby joined <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> and Jackie <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leeds_United" title="Leeds United">Leeds United</a> both contributing much to the success and history of their respective clubs. They both became permanent fixtures in <a href="/wiki/Alf_Ramsey" title="Alf Ramsey">Alf Ramsey's</a> 1966 England World Cup winning team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Macdonald" title="Malcolm Macdonald">Malcolm Macdonald</a> was a successful Newcastle player of the 1970s, goalscorers like McDonald often attract fame but Sunderland goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Montgomery" title="Jimmy Montgomery">Jim Montgomery's</a> double save, which helped Sunderland then a second Division club, beat at that time an all conquering Leeds United team to win the 1973 FA Cup Final by an <a href="/wiki/Ian_Porterfield" title="Ian Porterfield">Ian Porterfield</a> goal, is an incident that is frequently and fondly recalled. Great players of the 1980s and 1990s include local born internationals like <a href="/wiki/Peter_Beardsley" title="Peter Beardsley">Peter Beardsley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gascoigne" title="Paul Gascoigne">Paul Gascoigne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Waddle" title="Chris Waddle">Chris Waddle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a>. Shearer remains the highest scoring player in Premier League history with 260 goals in 441 appearances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> In the early 2000s Middlesbrough also joined the top clubs in English Football and played for a number of years in the Premier League and winning the League Cup in 2004. The Brazilian "<a href="/wiki/Juninho_Paulista" title="Juninho Paulista">Juninho Paulista</a>" was an influential player for Middlesbrough during their time in the top flight, a time when the <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> football academy became famous for producing a number of young top flight players such as <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Downing" title="Stewart Downing">Stewart Downing</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Morrison_(footballer)" title="James Morrison (footballer)">James Morrison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lee_Cattermole" title="Lee Cattermole">Lee Cattermole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Johnson_(footballer)" title="Adam Johnson (footballer)">Adam Johnson</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and, more recently, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Gibson" title="Ben Gibson">Ben Gibson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Horse_racing">Horse racing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Horse racing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Early races were mentioned in 1613 at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodham,_County_Durham" title="Woodham, County Durham">Woodham</a> near Aycliffe and were held at Newcastle's Killingworth Moor from 1632 before moving to the Town Moor. The 'Pitmen's Derby' or <a href="/wiki/Northumberland_Plate" title="Northumberland Plate">Northumberland Plate</a> was held from 1833 and moved to <a href="/wiki/Gosforth" title="Gosforth">Gosforth</a> in 1882. Georgian races were held at places like <a href="/wiki/Barnard_Castle" title="Barnard Castle">Barnard Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bishop_Auckland" title="Bishop Auckland">Bishop Auckland</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blaydon" title="Blaydon">Blaydon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chester-le-Street" title="Chester-le-Street">Chester-le-Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darlington" title="Darlington">Darlington</a>, Durham, Gateshead, <a href="/wiki/Hebburn" title="Hebburn">Hebburn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heighington,_County_Durham" title="Heighington, County Durham">Heighington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lanchester,_County_Durham" title="Lanchester, County Durham">Lanchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryton,_Tyne_and_Wear" title="Ryton, Tyne and Wear">Ryton</a>, Sedgefield, South Shields, Stockton-on-Tees, Sunderland, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tanfield,_Durham" title="Tanfield, Durham">Tanfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whickham" title="Whickham">Whickham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Witton_Gilbert" title="Witton Gilbert">Witton Gilbert</a>. A 1740 Act banned smaller meetings but some meetings like Durham survived into the late 19th or early 20th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Modern day horse racing is still popular and regular events still take place at Redcar, Newcastle and Sedgfield Race Courses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Blaydon_Races">Blaydon Races</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Blaydon Races">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Blaydon_Races" title="Blaydon Races">Blaydon Races</a>, a popular musical hall song first sung by Geordie Ridley at Balmbra's Music Hall in Newcastle in 1862, gives an idea of some of the characters attending the old meetings. These races were held on an island in the middle of the Tyne and were last held on 2 September 1916. A riot broke out after the winning horse was disqualified, and the event was discontinued. It is remembered in the famous English folk song The Blaydon Races, and the event and its characters are vividly depicted in William Irving's 1903 painting. 'The Blaydon Races – A Study from Life' which is on show at the <a href="/wiki/Shipley_Art_Gallery" title="Shipley Art Gallery">Shipley Art Gallery</a> in Gateshead.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Golf">Golf</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Golf">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Golf is a Scottish import to many countries but it is said to have been played in this region by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Cuthbert" title="St Cuthbert">St Cuthbert</a> on the dunes of the Northumberland coast. The oldest club in Northeast England was <a href="/wiki/Alnmouth" title="Alnmouth">Alnmouth</a> founded in 1869 – the fourth oldest in the country and is now Alnmouth Village Club and an interesting 9 hole links course.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> There are three fine old <a href="/wiki/Links_(golf)" title="Links (golf)">links</a> courses in this region at Seaton Carew, Goswick and Redcar.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%22The_Doctor%22_hole_at_Seaton_Carew_Colf_Club.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/%22The_Doctor%22_hole_at_Seaton_Carew_Colf_Club.jpg/250px-%22The_Doctor%22_hole_at_Seaton_Carew_Colf_Club.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/%22The_Doctor%22_hole_at_Seaton_Carew_Colf_Club.jpg/375px-%22The_Doctor%22_hole_at_Seaton_Carew_Colf_Club.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/%22The_Doctor%22_hole_at_Seaton_Carew_Colf_Club.jpg/500px-%22The_Doctor%22_hole_at_Seaton_Carew_Colf_Club.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%22The_Doctor%22_hole_at_Seaton_Carew_Colf_Club.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"The Doctor", a testing golf hole named after Dr McCuaig, founder of Seaton Carew Golf Club. (par 3 encircled by 8 bunkers)</div></div></div>
<p>The first golf course appeared in County Durham in 1874<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hornby_1974_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hornby_1974-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trotter_2001_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trotter_2001-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> at <a href="/wiki/Seaton_Carew_Golf_Club" title="Seaton Carew Golf Club">Seaton Carew Golf Club</a> near Hartlepool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> It was to become the only course in the whole of the counties of Durham and <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a> and was originally called the Durham and Yorkshire Golf Club and reference to this today remains in the Club's badge. Seaton Carew is the 10th oldest Golf Club in England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The Club was set up by a newly qualified surgeon from Edinburgh, who played at Musselburgh, when he realised there was nowhere for him to continue to practice his passion for the game. This was Dr. Duncan McCuaig, who had moved down to Teesside shortly after qualifying at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a>. His memory can be recalled when one plays the third hole, a challenging par 3, named "The Doctor". Over the years some of the finest golfers in the country have played the links at Seaton Carew, including the legendary "<a href="/wiki/Great_Triumvirate_(golf)" title="Great Triumvirate (golf)">Great Triumvirate</a>" of Golf <a href="/wiki/Harry_Vardon" title="Harry Vardon">Harry Vardon</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Henry_Taylor" title="John Henry Taylor">John Henry "J H" Taylor</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Braid_(golfer)" title="James Braid (golfer)">James Braid</a> and several other Open Champions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hornby_1974_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hornby_1974-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trotter_2001_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-Trotter_2001-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Alister_MacKenzie" title="Alister MacKenzie">Dr Alister MacKenzie</a>, the designer of <a href="/wiki/Augusta_National_Golf_Club" title="Augusta National Golf Club">Augusta National Golf Club</a> in <a href="/wiki/Augusta,_Georgia" title="Augusta, Georgia">Augusta, Georgia</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Masters_Tournament" title="Masters Tournament">The Masters</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cypress_Point_Club" title="Cypress Point Club">Cypress Point</a> golf course in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, lengthened the Seaton Carew Course in 1925 to 6,500 yards and designed new holes eastwards including the planting of over 2,000 buckthorn bushes. In 1937, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Hagen" title="Walter Hagen">Walter Hagen</a> played an exhibition match at Seaton Carew during a tour of Europe and commented "It is a splendid course, the links are well groomed. It is not an easy course and provides a good test of golf. It is one I would like to play quite often".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> This Club by varying the playing sequence of the 22 holes can create 5 different course layouts. In 2014, "flyovers" of all 5 Seaton Carew Golf Course layouts were created with commentaries by well known golf TV commentator <a href="/wiki/Peter_Alliss" title="Peter Alliss">Peter Alliss</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Alliss comments: "The tenth oldest in England and a true championship links to challenge all levels of players." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>Seaton Carew Golf Club is regular host to top amateur golf competitions. Golf England's <a href="/wiki/Brabazon_Trophy" title="Brabazon Trophy">Brabazon Trophy</a> was held at this Club in 1985 and the winner, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Baker_(golfer)" title="Peter Baker (golfer)">Peter Baker</a>, went on to Ryder Cup and European Tour success after sharing this amateur title with the North East's Roger Roper (Roper famously turned professional at the age of 50 in 2007 to compete on the Seniors Professional Tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup>) The 2013 US Open Champion <a href="/wiki/Justin_Rose" title="Justin Rose">Justin Rose</a> talked glowingly about Seaton's undulating links course when in 1966 he came second behind the then amateur, now established tour professional <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Storm" title="Graeme Storm">Graeme Storm</a> from Hartlepool, in the Carris Trophy (the Boys' equivalent to the Brabazon Trophy). In June 2014, The Brabazon Trophy tournament returned to Seaton Carew and in line with the illustrious outcomes for past winners on this course a bright future is predicted for the winner Ben Stow from Wiltshire. Stow equalled the course record on the final day with a "birdie" on the final hole to win the Barabzon Trophy by one shot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Goswick" title="Goswick">Goswick</a> near Berwick on Tweed is a James Braid design masterpiece which is widely acknowledged as a classic Northumberland links Golf course,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> so much so, that the Royal and Ancient Golf Club (R&amp;A) chose Goswick as a regional qualifier for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_Championship" title="Open Championship">Open Championship</a> for five years from 2008. At <a href="/wiki/Redcar" title="Redcar">Redcar</a> on Teesside, the <a class="external text" href="http://www.clevelandgolfclub.co.uk/" rel="nofollow">Cleveland Golf Course</a> of 1887 is the oldest in Yorkshire. The Tyneside Golf Club at <a href="/wiki/Ryton,_Tyne_and_Wear" title="Ryton, Tyne and Wear">Ryton</a> dates from 1880 but there may have been earlier courses in the region. During the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a> of 1642–1651, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Charles_I_of_England" title="King Charles I of England">King Charles</a> played 'Goff' in the Shield Fields of the suburb of Pandon near Newcastle during his imprisonment in the town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p><p>Today inland golf courses are abundant in the northeast of England,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> <a class="external text" href="http://www.middlesbroughgolfclub.co.uk/" rel="nofollow">Middlesbrough's Brass Castle Golf Club</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brancepeth" title="Brancepeth">Brancepeth</a> Golf Club being two excellent examples from many but those new courses created in the late 20th and early 21st centuries at <a href="/wiki/Wynyard_Golf_Club" title="Wynyard Golf Club">Wynyard</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.rockliffehall.com/golf/index.aspx" rel="nofollow">Rockciffe Hall</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.devere-hotels.co.uk/hotel-lodges/locations/slaley-hall/contact-us.html" rel="nofollow">Slalely Hall</a>  and <a class="external text" href="http://www.closehouse.co.uk/golf/" rel="nofollow">Close House</a> have rapidly gained an international reputation and regularly hold professional events such as the Seve Trophy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> and the Seniors Tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>
</p><p>The region has two professional golfers who are currently prominent in many professional golf tour events: <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Ferrie" title="Kenneth Ferrie">Kenny Ferrie</a> from <a href="/wiki/Ashington" title="Ashington">Ashington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Storm" title="Graeme Storm">Graeme Storm</a> from Hartlepool have both won events on the prestigious <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Tour" title="European Tour">European Tour</a>.
</p><p>The largest corporate golf day in the United Kingdom is held annually each September by the members of the Northeast of England Process Industry Cluster (NEPIC) when 180 golfers play both the Slaley Hunting and Priestman courses simultaneously, after a shot gun start.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_East_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Cricket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Riverside-ground.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="723" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Riverside-ground.jpg/220px-Riverside-ground.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Riverside-ground.jpg/330px-Riverside-ground.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Riverside-ground.jpg/440px-Riverside-ground.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Riverside-ground.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Riverside Ground, Chester-le-Street</div></div></div>
<p>Cricket has long been a popular sport in the Northeast of England and is said to date back to Elizabethan times. <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Yorkshire County Cricket Club">Yorkshire County Cricket Club</a> was formed in 1863 and Durham County Cricket Club in 1882. After many years of success in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minor_Counties_Championship" title="Minor Counties Championship">Minor Counties Championship</a>, Durham joined Yorkshire in the senior counties championship in 1992. The Riverside cricket stadium, the home of <a href="/wiki/Durham_County_Cricket_Club" title="Durham County Cricket Club">Durham County Cricket Club</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> in Chester-le-Street, in full view of Lumley Castle, is now one of the most picturesque cricket venues in the UK.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This venue now regularly hosts international cricket; its first "Ashes" Test Match between England and Australia was in August 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> With 320 runs and 15 wickets on the last day of the match, the venue provided "the most high-octane day of a thrilling Test match", and England took an unassailable 3-0 lead against the Australians in the five-match Ashes Test series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
